        <h6 class="cp-kicker"></h6>
        <h2 class="cp-celeb" itemprop="headline name">
    <a href="http://www.nytimes.com/interactive/projects/cp/oscars-2015/show/penns-green-card-joke-gets-a-laugh-from-inarritu" itemprop="url">Penn's Green Card Joke Gets a Laugh From Iñárritu</a>
</h2>

        <figcaption class="cp-desc" itemprop="articleBody caption description text">
            <p>As he was presenting the best picture Oscar for “Birdman” to the Mexican director Alejandro G. Iñárritu, Sean Penn joked, or tried to, “Who gave this son of a bitch a green card?”</p><p>The show was ticking past midnight, and Mr. Iñárritu took the stage and went for the save: “Two Mexicans in a row. That’s suspicious, I guess,” he responded.</p><p>The remark by Mr. Penn, a star of Mr. Iñárritu’s 2003 film “21 Grams,” did not go over well in many quarters, but backstage the director said he wasn’t offended. “I found it hilarious,” he said, adding “Sean and I have that kind of brutal relationship. I think it was very funny.”</p>
        </figcaption>
        <ul class="cp-related">
</ul>
            <div class="tone-standard sharetools theme-classic sharetools-story-meta layout-horizontal" 
   
  aria-label="tools" role="group"

  data-description="As he was presenting the best picture Oscar for “Birdman” to the Mexican director Alejandro G. Iñárritu, Sean Penn joked, or tried to, “Who gave this son of a bitch a green card?”

The show was ticking past midnight, and Mr. Iñárritu took the stage and went for the save: “Two Mexicans in a row. That’s suspicious, I guess,” he responded.

The remark by Mr. Penn, a star of Mr. Iñárritu’s 2003 film “21 Grams,” did not go over well in many quarters, but backstage the director said he wasn’t offended. “I found it hilarious,” he said, adding “Sean and I have that kind of brutal relationship. I think it was very funny.”
"

			<div id="nytmm_extra_about" class="nytmm_extra_info outofview">
				<div class="content">
					<h4>About the Project</h4>
					<p>&ldquo;A Short History of the Highrise&rdquo; is an interactive documentary that explores the 2,500-year global history of vertical living and issues of social equality in an increasingly urbanized world. The centerpiece of the project is four short films. The first three (&ldquo;Mud,&rdquo; &ldquo;Concrete&rdquo; and &ldquo;Glass&rdquo;) draw on the New York Times&rsquo;s extraordinary visual archives, a repository of millions of photographs that have largely been unseen in decades. Each film is intended to evoke a chapter in a storybook, with rhyming narration and photographs brought to life with intricate animation. The fourth chapter (&ldquo;Home&rdquo;) comprises images submitted by the public. The interactive experience incorporates the films and, like a visual accordion, allows viewers to dig deeper into the project&rsquo;s themes with additional archival materials, text and miniature games. On tablets, viewers can navigate the story extras and special features within the films using touch commands like swipe, pinch, pull and tap. On desktop and laptop computers, users can mouse over features and click to navigate. Smartphone users can view the four films.</p><p>This project was created for <a href="http://www.nytimes.com/opdocs" id="opdocs_link" target="_blank">Op-Docs</a>, the New York Times editorial department&rsquo;s forum for short, opinionated documentaries, and is part of the National Film Board of Canada&rsquo;s ongoing <a href="http://highrise.nfb.ca/" id="highrise_link"  target="_blank">HIGHRISE</a> project, an Emmy Award-winning multiyear, many-media collaborative documentary experiment. <a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2013/10/08/opinion/a-short-history-of-the-highrise.html" id="statement_link" target="_blank">Read More &raquo;</a></p>
					<div class="nytmm_fullvideo_promo clearfix">
						<div class="nytmm_fullvideo_poster">
							<a href="http://www.nytimes.com/video/2013/10/03/opinion/100000002480449/a-short-history-of-the-morgue.html" target="_blank">
								<img src="http://graphics8.nytimes.com/images/2013/10/03/opinion/video-opdoc-morgue/video-opdoc-morgue-sfSpan.jpg">
							</a>
						</div>
						<div class="nytmm_fullvideo_text">
							<h4>Behind the Scenes Video</h4>
							<h3><a href="http://www.nytimes.com/video/2013/10/03/opinion/100000002480449/a-short-history-of-the-morgue.html" target="_blank">A Short History of the Morgue</a></h3>
							<p>Inside the New York Times photo archives, known as the &ldquo;morgue,&rdquo; the filmmaker Katerina Cizek and the archivist Jeff Roth discuss the making of &ldquo;A Short History of the Highrise.&rdquo;</p>
						</div>

<h1>Princelings</h1>

<div class="topicUpdateDigestHeader">
<table><tr><td>
<h1 id="title">Princelings</h1>
</td><td>
<h2 id="subtitle">A series that looks at how relatives of top Chinese officials have amassed vast wealth through businesses closely entwined with the state. The series won <a href="http://www.pulitzer.org/citation/2013-International-Reporting">a Pulitzer Prize for international reporting</a> on April 15, 2013.</h2>
</td></tr></table>
<div class="clear"><!----></div>
</div>
<div class="clear"><!----></div>
<div class="topicUpdateDigestWrapper">
<div class="topicUpdateDigest">
<p class="leadIn"></p>
<div class="update updateFirst"> 
<p class="updateLabel"> 
<a name="May_18,_2012">May 18, 2012</a> 
</p>
<div class="block blockFull"> 
<div class="contentColumn contentColumnLast"> 
<div class="contentFull contentFirst"> 
<div class="content">
<div class="imgWrapper">
<a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2012/05/18/world/asia/china-princelings-using-family-ties-to-gain-riches.html">
<div class="imgCtnt">
<img src="http://graphics8.nytimes.com/images/2012/12/19/business/princelings-landing-page/princelings-landing-page-jumbo.jpg"/> 
</div>
</a>
<p class="credit"></p>
<p class="caption">Family members of many high-ranking officials have profited enormously from China&rsquo;s economic boom.</p>
</div>
<h3>
<a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2012/05/18/world/asia/china-princelings-using-family-ties-to-gain-riches.html">&lsquo;Princelings&rsquo; in China Use Family Ties to Gain Riches</a>
</h3>
<p class="byline">By <span>David Barboza and Sharon LaFraniere</span></p>
<p class="lead">Evidence is mounting that the relatives of many current and former senior officials in China have amassed vast wealth, often playing central roles in businesses closely entwined with the state, including those involved in finance, energy, domestic security, telecommunications and entertainment. Many of these so-called princelings also serve as middlemen to a host of global companies and wealthy tycoons eager to do business in China.</p>
<div class="clear"></div>
</div> 
</div>
<div class="clear"></div> 
</div>
<div class="clear"></div> 
</div> 
</div>
<div class="update "> 
<p class="updateLabel"> 
<a name="Oct._26,_2012">Oct. 26, 2012</a> 
</p>
<div class="block blockFull"> 
<div class="contentColumn contentColumnLast"> 
<div class="contentFull "> 
<div class="content">
<div class="imgWrapper">
<a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2012/10/26/business/global/family-of-wen-jiabao-holds-a-hidden-fortune-in-china.html?pagewanted=all"> 
<div class="imgCtnt">
<img src="http://graphics8.nytimes.com/images/2012/10/25/world/asia/20121026-WEN-slide-6CG7/20121026-WEN-slide-6CG7-articleInline.jpg"/> 
</div> 
</a>
<p class="credit">Petar Kujundzic/Reuters</p>
</div>
<h3>
<a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2012/10/26/business/global/family-of-wen-jiabao-holds-a-hidden-fortune-in-china.html">Billions in Hidden Riches for Family of Chinese Leader</a>
</h3>
<p class="byline">By <span>David Barboza</span></p>
<p class="lead">A review of corporate and regulatory records by The New York Times indicates that the relatives of China's prime minister, Wen Jiabao &mdash; some of whom, including his wife, have a knack for aggressive deal making &mdash; have controlled assets worth at least $2.7 billion. Untangling their financial holdings provides an unusually detailed look at how politically connected people have profited from being at the intersection of government and business as state influence and private wealth converge in China&rsquo;s fast-growing economy.</p>
<ul class="headlinesOnly">
<li>
<h5>
<a href="http://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2012/10/25/business/the-wen-family-empire.html">
<img src="http://graphics8.nytimes.com/images/multimedia/icons/interactive_icon.gif" />
Graphic: The Wen Family Empire										</a>
</h5>
</li>
<li>
<h5>
<a href="http://cn.nytimes.com/article/china/2012/10/26/c26princeling/">
Chinese Translation of Article										</a>
</h5>
</li>
<li>
<h5>
<a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2012/10/27/business/global/obtaining-financial-records-in-china.html">
Related: Obtaining Financial Records in China										</a>
</h5>
</li>
</ul>
<div class="clear"></div>
</div> 
</div>
<div class="clear"></div> 
</div>
<div class="clear"></div> 
</div> 
</div>
<div class="update "> 
<p class="updateLabel"> 
<a name="Nov._25,_2012">Nov. 25, 2012</a> 
</p>
<div class="block blockFull"> 
<div class="contentColumn contentColumnLast"> 
<div class="contentFull "> 
<div class="content">
<div class="imgWrapper">
<a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2012/11/25/business/chinese-insurers-regulatory-win-benefits-a-leaders-family.html?pagewanted=all"> 
<div class="imgCtnt">
<img src="http://graphics8.nytimes.com/images/2012/11/25/world/jp-china-1/jp-china-1-articleInline.jpg"/> 
</div> 
</a>
<p class="credit">The New York Times</p>
</div>
<h3>
<a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2012/11/25/business/chinese-insurers-regulatory-win-benefits-a-leaders-family.html?pagewanted=all">Lobbying, a Windfall and a Leader&rsquo;s Family</a>
</h3>
<p class="byline">By <span>David Barboza</span></p>
<p class="lead">The greatest source of wealth for the relatives of Wen Jiabao, the prime minister of China, came from the shares in Ping An bought about eight months after the insurer was granted a waiver to the requirement that big financial companies be broken up. Long before most investors could buy Ping An stock, Taihong, a company that would soon be controlled by Mr. Wen&rsquo;s relatives, acquired a large stake in Ping An from state-owned entities that held shares in the insurer, regulatory and corporate records show. And by all appearances, Taihong got a sweet deal.</p>
<ul class="headlinesOnly">
<li>
<h5>
<a href="http://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2012/11/25/business/ping-ans-hidden-shareholders-friends-and-family-of-wen-jiabao.html?ref=business">
<img src="http://graphics8.nytimes.com/images/multimedia/icons/interactive_icon.gif" />
Graphic: Ping An&rsquo;s Hidden Shareholders &mdash; Friends and Family of Wen Jiabao										</a>
</h5>
</li>
<li>
<h5>
<a href="http://cn.nytimes.com/article/china/2012/11/27/c27pingan/">
Chinese Translation of Article										</a>
</h5>
</li>
<li>
<h5>
<a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2012/11/25/business/global/another-big-stake-in-ping-an-hidden-in-a-hong-kong-investment.html">
Related: Another Big Stake in Ping An Hidden in a Hong Kong Investment										</a>
</h5>
</li>

<p class="updateLabel"> 
<a name="December_31,_2012">December 31, 2012</a> 
</p>
<div class="block blockFull"> 
<div class="contentColumn contentColumnLast"> 
<div class="contentFull "> 
<div class="content">
<div class="imgWrapper">
<a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2012/12/31/business/global/chinese-regulators-family-profited-from-stake-in-insurer.html"> 
<div class="imgCtnt">
<img src="http://graphics8.nytimes.com/images/2012/12/31/business/jp31Banker1/jp31Banker1-articleInline-v2.jpg?ts=1356924148918"/> 
</div> 
</a>
<p class="credit">The New York Times</p>
</div>
<h3>
<a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2012/12/31/business/global/chinese-regulators-family-profited-from-stake-in-insurer.html">Chinese Regulator&rsquo;s Family Reaps Insurance Profit</a>
</h3>
<p class="byline">By <span>David Barboza</span></p>
<p class="lead">Relatives of a top Chinese regulator profited enormously from the purchase of shares in a once-struggling insurance company that is now one of China&rsquo;s biggest financial powerhouses, according to interviews and a review of regulatory filings. The regulator, Dai Xianglong, was the head of China&rsquo;s central bank and also had oversight of the insurance industry in 2002, when a company his relatives helped control bought a big stake in Ping An Insurance that years later came to be worth billions of dollars. The insurer was drawing new investors ahead of a public stock offering after averting insolvency a few years earlier.</p>
<ul class="headlinesOnly">
<li>
<h5>
<a href="http://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2012/12/31/business/global/lucrative-stock-sale.html">
<img src="http://graphics8.nytimes.com/images/multimedia/icons/graphic_icon.gif" />
Graphic: A Lucrative Stock Sale										</a>
</h5>
</li>
</ul>
<div class="clear"></div>
</div> 
</div>
<div class="clear"></div> 
</div>
<div class="clear"></div> 
</div> 
</div>
</div>
<div class="topicUpdateDigestSideBar">
<div class="sideBarCtnt">
<div class="freeform">
<p class="intro">Comments</p>				<div class="story comment">
<p class="lead">I can see the body of Mao spinning in his glass coffin in Beijing right now. So much for the communist ideal of everyone is equal and everyone shares in the wealth of the state.
</p>
<h5><a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2012/10/26/business/global/family-of-wen-jiabao-holds-a-hidden-fortune-in-china.html?comments#permid=17"> Nick Metrowsky &middot; Longmont, Colo.</a>
</h5>
</div>
<div class="story comment">
<p class="lead">My experience in China has taught me that nothing happens there without some party official profiting from it. The second thing I have learned is that this is culturally accepted as the engine of progress. 
</p>
<h5><a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2012/10/26/business/global/family-of-wen-jiabao-holds-a-hidden-fortune-in-china.html?comments#permid=146"> tosten &middot; Swan Valley, Mont. </a>
</h5>
</div>
<div class="story comment">
<p class="lead">Insiders are such a pernicious bane of capitalist economies. They are even worse in a situation like China where insiders can hide behind political power structures.
</p>
<h5><a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2012/11/25/business/chinese-insurers-regulatory-win-benefits-a-leaders-family.html?comments#permid=23">     c harris &middot; Rock Hill, S.C. </a>
</h5>
</div>
<div class="story comment">
<p class="lead">I am a citizen of China. I just want to thank the press of NYTimes for providing such in-depth investigation and report.
</p>
<h5><a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2012/11/25/business/chinese-insurers-regulatory-win-benefits-a-leaders-family.html?comments#permid=64">scidem &middot; New York, N.Y. </a>
</h5>
</div>
<div class="story comment">
<p class="lead">The children of powerful people have always found ways to cash in on their family connections. There is nothing newsworthy about it. This is how human societies operate.
</p>
<h5><a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2012/05/18/world/asia/china-princelings-using-family-ties-to-gain-riches.html?comments#permid=51">mingsphinx &middot; Singapore </a>
</h5>
</div>
<div class="story comment">
<p class="lead">It constantly amazes me how the societies that attempted to change themselves through Marxist revolution end up not changing at all.
</p>
<h5><a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2012/05/18/world/asia/china-princelings-using-family-ties-to-gain-riches.html?comments#permid=46">James Hadley &middot; Orleans, Mass. </a>
</h5>
</div>					</div>
